Kühn, Leipzig, 1821-33) de febrium differentiis II 9 (VII 367), de pulsum differentia IV 10-11 (VIII 748-54), de dignoscendis pulsibus I 3 (VIII 787), IV 2 (VIII 935-37), de venae sectione adversus Erasistratum 5 (XI 163), de compositione medicamentorum per genera V 11 (XIII 830), Hippocratis Epidemion I et Galeni in illum commentarius II 25 (XVII 1, 120), Hippocratis Epidemion VI et Galeni in illum commentarius II 26 (XVII 1, 942-43), definitiones medicae 14 (XIX 353); vita A. Ἀγησανδρίδας

LATE V BC

  • Poralla 5; Thucydides VIII 91.2, 94-5a, 107b; Diodorus XIII 41c; Xenophon Hellenica I 1.1d, 3.17e
  • Son of Agesandros
  • Brother of Pasitelidas

  • After the battle of Cynossema he went to the Hellespont under the orders of the nauarch Mindares, but was shipwrecked near Athos.bc With the ships that were saved he defeated the Athenian Thymochares.d
  • In 409/8 he was in Thrace.e

Ἀγησίλαος II

444/3-360/59 BC

  • Poralla 9; Diodorus 14.80a, 15.31-34b, 82.6-83.5c, 92-3d; Nepos Agesilaus (8e), Timotheus 1.3f, Conon 2, Chabrias 1,2, de regibus 1; Pausanias III 8.8ffg, 9.1-5h, IV 17.5, VI 4.9, 15.7, VIII 6.2, IX 13.2, 14.5; Plutarch Agesilaus (1i, 3j, 6k, 7-13l, 17-19m, 20n, 21o, 22p, 27-8q, 31-33r, 34s, 36-40t), Lysander 22u, 24v, Lycurgus 30.5, Artaxerxes 22.4-7, Moralia (de audiendis poetis) 31c, (de adulatore et amico) 52f, 55d, (de profectibus in virtute) 78d, 81a, 85b, (regum et imperatorum apophthegmata) 189e, (apophthegmata Laconica) 208b-215a, 229f, (parallela Graeca et Romana) 308b, (de Alexandri fortuna) 343a, (de Pythiae oraculis) 399b, (de fraterno amore) 482d, (de vitioso pudore) 533e-534b, (de laude ipsius) 545a, (de genio Socratis) 577e, 578f, (quaestionum convivalium II 10.2) 644b, (an seni sit gerenda res puiblica) 784ef, 790b, (praecepta gerendae reipublicae) 805e, 807e, 809a/b, (non posse suaviter vivi secundum Epicurum) 1099b; Hellenica Oxyrhyncus 11.2-5, 12.1-4, 13.1, 21.1-4, 22.2,4w; Xenophon Agesilaus (1.25-35x; 2.17y, 21z, 26-7A, 9.6B); Hellenica C III 3-4 passim; IV-VI passim, VII 5.9, 10; Aristotle Politica 1306b35; SEG XI 457 (father?); Libanius declamationes XXIV 2 (mel): 6; Isocrates epistulae IX 11-14, orationes IV 144, 153, V 62, 86, 87; Athenaeus IV 144b, IX 384a, XII 511c, 550e, XIII 609b, XIV 613c, 616d, 657b; Josephus Bellum Judaicum II 359; Diogenes Laertius II 51, 52, 57, VI 39, VIII 87; Die Inschriften von Ephesos (der Österreichischen Akademie der Wissenschaften) II 133
  • Eurypontid king
  • Son of King Archidamos II and Eupolia
  • Half-brother of King Agis II and Teleutias
  • Brother of KyniskainoB
  • Agesilaos was born in 444/3 and about 402 married Kleora (cf. Aristomenidas) who bore him three children, Archidamos, Eupolia, and Prolyta.mC
  • When, after the death of Agis II in the summer of 399, Agis’ son Leotychidas was disqualified, Agesilaos—particularly through the influence of his boyhood friend Lysander—received the throne.Cujg
  • Likewise, through the efforts of Lysander was Agesilaos appointed the commander in the war against Persia. He sailed in the spring of 396 from Aulis to Ephesus.kCh
  • He conducted the war in Asia Minor until the summer of 394, when he was recalled because of political developments in Greece.Cxwlva
  • In thirty days he marched to Boeotia, where he established a camp at Chaeroneia on the 25th or 26th of August 394 and soon thereafter defeated the enemies of Sparta in the battle of Coronea.Cm
  • To heal the wound that he had received in the battle he took himself to Delphi and from there travelled home on a ship.Cx
  • In 391 he laid waste to Argos and continued on to Corinth where he had the long walls of Lechaeum torn down.Cy
  • In the summer of the next year <390> he was active at the IsthmusCop. There he fought on behalf of the Achaeans against the Acarnanians.Cp
  • At the peace conference in Sparta in 387/6 he forced through the recognition of the King’s Peace on the part of the Thebans and the dissolution of the just founded city Corinth-Argos.Cz
  • In the fall of 381 he struck against Phlius, which he took after a siege of twenty months.C
  • In similar fashion he participated in the great struggle between Thebes and Sparta. He undertook two operations to Boeotia in 378/7. A wound, which he received on the march back, kept him from the theater of war for a long time,Cb so he acted all the more energetically against Thebes in 371 at the congress at Sparta, when he excluded the Thebans from the common peace.Cq
  • After the catastrophe at Leuctra he campaigned with the full army against Mantinea, but had to withdraw to Sparta at the approach of the Thebans.C By his careful handling he saved the country from the invasion of Epaminondas in the winter of 370/69.r
  • Around 364 he travelled to Asia to earn money for Sparta and fought there together with the Athenian Timotheos for the interests of Ariobarzanes.Af
  • In 362 we find the king back in Greece, where shortly before the battle of Mantinea he saved Sparta a second time from a Theban invasion.Csc
  • In 361 he went to Egypt to enter the service of Tachos, to earn money for Sparta as the leader of a mercenary band. When he was demoted by Tachos he went over to Nectanebo and did important service for him. Therefore, when he prepared his return home, he was loaded with rich gifts. He never reached his homeland, but died in the winter of 360/59 between Egypt and Cyrene in the “harbor of Menelaos.” His body was brought back to Sparta.tde

Ἀγησίπολις I

V\IV BC

  • Poralla 14; Diodorus XIV 89a, XV 22,2, 23,2b; Pausanias III 5.7c, VIII 8.7-9(f); Xenophon Hellenica IV 2.9d, 7.2-7e; V 2.3-7f, 3.8-9, 18-9g (Agesipolis and Agesilaus have been confused in Suidas s. v. Ἆγις and Diodorus XIV 97.5.)
  • Agid king
  • Son of King Pausanias
  • Brother of Kleombrotos
  • When his father went into exile after the battle of Haliartos in 395, Agesipolis ascended the throneac. Since he was still a minor, he had a regent, Aristodemusd.
  • In 388/7 he led a successful campaign against the Argivese. In 385/4 he forced Mantinea to disband the league it had formedf. In the year 381 he invaded Chalcidice with a great army, but died shortly after the capture of Torone in Summer 380.
  • His body was brought to Spartabg.

  • Agid kinga
  • After the death of his father in 371 Agesipolis succeeded to the throne, but he died after about a one-year reign and left no childrenabc.

  • 219 BCab His uncle, Kleomenes (2), was regenta. He was expelled by Lykourgos (1)c. As an envoy to Rome, ca. 184 BC, he was killed by piratesb.

Ἀγητορίδας (1)

FIRST HALF IV BC

  • Poralla 19; Plutarch Moralia (de genio Socratis 7) 578e
  • A Spartiate who was sent by Agesilaos II to Memphis during the time when Plato was travelling in Egypt. We do not have an exact date for Plato’s Egyptian stay. Plato left Athens after the death of Socrates and travelled through the Peloponnesus, to Egypt and Cyrene. In 388 he had already visited Syracuse again. The trip of Agetoridas then, if it is at all historical, must fall in the period 399-388.

Ἁγίας

VI\V BC

  • Poralla 21; Herodotus IX 33 (the name is known in the Ionian form:
  • Ἡγίης)
  • Son of the Elean Antiochos
  • Brother of the famous Elean seer Tisamenos.
  • Along with his brother he received Spartan citizenship shortly before the battle of Marathon.

Ἁγίας

END V BC

  • Poralla 22; Pausanias III 11. 5-6, X 9.7 (where his name is written Ἄβας)
  • Son of Agelochos
  • He belonged to the Elean family of seers which had been given citizenship in Sparta around 480. He took part in the battle of Aegospotami. (cf. Τισαμενός stemma)

Ἁγίας

Ἀγιᾶτις

DIED ca. 224 BC

  • Plutarch Cleomenes 1.1-3, 22.1-3, [Aratus 39.3]
  • Daughter of Gylippos (1)
  • Wife of Agis (1) IV and mother of a son by him
  • Wife of Kleomenes (1) III and mother of at least two sons by him
  • (Cleom. 38.3)
  • She was a wealthy woman. After the death of Agis IV, Leonidas (1) II forced her to marry his son, Kleomenes, so that her wealth would not pass to another. She was supposed to have encouraged Kleomenes in his reforms.

Ἆγις I

HEROIC AGE

  • Poralla 25; Herodotus I 65a, VII 204b; Strabo VIII 365c; Pausanias III 16.9d
  • Son of Eurysthenesab
  • Father of Echestratos and, according to one version, of the lawgiver Lycurgusab.
  • He was the eponymous king of the house of the Agids—obviously a mythical personab.
  • During his reign (1061-1030/29) the helots were subjugatedc. He is also made the ultimate ancestor of the mythical Amphiklesd.

Ἆγις II

DIED 399 BC

  • Poralla 26; Thucydides III 89a, IV 2. 6b, V 19, 24c, 54d, 57-60 & 63-75e, 83f, VII 19 & 27g, VIII 3h, 5-11 & 70-71i; Plutarch Agesilaus 1. 3j; Diodorus XI 48k, XII 35.4l, 78-79m, XIII 107n; Xenophon Hellenica I 1.33-35o, II 2. 7-13p, II 3.3q, III 2.22-29 & 3.1r; Pausanias III 8.3-5s, VI 2.3t; IDelos 87 (IG V 1. 1564); Justin V 2.5; Nepos Agesilaus 1; Athenaeus XII 535b, 543b
  • King from the house of the Eurypontids
  • Son of Archidamos II
  • Step brother of Agesilaos II
  • Father of Leotychidas (by Timaia)j.
  • After the death of Archidamos Agis assumed the throne in 427/6k. In the years 426 and 425 he twice led the army into Attica.ab With his fellow king Pleistoanax in 421 he underwrote the peace of Nicias and the alliance with Athens.c
  • In 419 he marched with the assembled army to Leuctra, but turned back to Sparta without accomplishing anything.d In the next summer he campaigned twice against the Argives and besieged them because of their alliance with Mantineaem. In a third campaign at the beginning of the winter of 417 he caused the newly built walls of Argos to be torn downf.
  • In spring 413 Agis invaded Attica and seized Decelea, where he remained as commanderg. From here he undertook in the following winter a campaign against the Oitaians and the Achaeans living in Phthiotis, to reestablish the influence of the Spartans on the Malean Gulfh. From Decelea Agis supported all rebellions against Athens in Asia Minor and along the Hellespont and tried several times to take the cityio. He did not take part in the siege of Athens in 405/4nq, although he did offer his good ofices to the Atheniansp.
  • After the fall of Athens he led a long campaign against Elist and visited Delphi. On his return trip he fell sick and died soon after his arrival in Sparta, probably in the summer of 399lrs.

Ἆγις III

DIED 330 BC

  • Poralla 27; Plutarch Agis 3a; Pausanias III 10.5b; Arrian Anabasis II 13.6c; Diodorus XVI 88.4d, XVII 48.1-2e, 62.6-63.4f; Curtius VI 1g
  • Eurypontid king
  • Son of Archidamos III
  • Brother of Eudamidas and Agesilaosabc
  • He succeeded his father in 338 and ruled for nine yearsd. In 333, as leader of the opposition to Alexander the Great, Agis travelled to Siphnos to meet Pharnabazos and Autophradates, the commanders of the Persian fleet; he obtained money and troops from them. Then he travelled to Halicarnassos where he led some of the survivors of the Greek mercenaries from the battle of Issos to Cretece. After he returned to Sparta he besieged Megalopolis, but in a battle fought there against Antipater, he was killed (in 331 or 330)fg.
  • Agis left no descendantsa.

Ἆγις

MID IV BC

  • Poralla 28; Nikandros Anthologia Palatina VII 435
  • Son of Iphikratidas and Alexippa
  • He and his brothers (Eupylidas, Chairis, Lykos, Alexon, Eraton, and Gylippos) fell at Messene sometime after 369.

Ἆγις, Poralla 28a; Herodotus VI 65, cf. Ἀγησίλαος (Poralla 10)

Ἆγις, Poralla 28b; Suidas s. v., cf. Ἀγησίπολις I

Ἆγις ( = III?)

Ἆγις (1) IV

DIED 241 BC

  • Plutarch Agis passim, Cleomenes 1-3, Agesilaus 40.5; comparatio Agis Cleomenes Ti. Gracchus C. Gracchus, Aratus 31.1; Moralia (apophthegmata Laconica) 216d; Lamprias catalogue Number 9; Cicero de officiis II 80; Pausanias II 8.5; III 10.5; VI 2.4; VII 7.3; VIII 8.11, 10.5-8, 27.13-14, 36.6 (Pausanias confuses Agis IV and Archidamos IV); Prometheus VII 1981, pp. 35-42: Agis became king as a child with Agesilaos as his regent.
  • Son of Eudamidas (2) II and Agesistrata
  • Father of [Eurydamidas (Pausanias III 10.5)]
  • Husband of Agiatis
  • Eurypontid king of Sparta
  • He was the first king of Sparta to attempt to recover her military strength through an increase in the number of citizen-soldiers by cancellation of debt, distribution of land, and enfranchisement.
  • He was opposed by the wealthy and by Leonidas (1) II, the Agiad king, though a large minority of the fully enfranchised citizen body supported Agis.
  • With the help of his advisers and supporters, Lysandros (1), Mandrokleidas, and Agesilaos (2), he expelled Leonidas, brought Kleombrotos (1) II to the throne, and passed a bill cancelling debt.
  • He led an army to aid the Achaean League against the Aetolians, but no engagement was fought. In his absence his opponents gained the upper hand. (Pausanias confuses the actions of the Aetolians and the Spartans under Agis in his reading of Plutarch’s life of Aratus.)
  • Leonidas II returned from exile and forced Agis to seek sanctuary. Agis was betrayed, tried by the ephors, and executed.

Ἀκρότατος (1)

MID IV BC

  • Diodorus Siculus XIX 70.4-71.6a, [XX 29.1]; Pausanias I 13.5, III 6.2, {VIII 27.11-13, VIII 30.7 by name refers to Akrotatos (1) but in fact refers to Akrotatos (2)}; Plutarch Agis 3.6b, Moralia (apophthegmata Laconica) 216de, 240ef (grandson of Gyrtias); SEG XI 668(?); SEG XXV 444; IOlymp, Number 308; ICret II xxiii 12A; {SIG3 430, see Akrotatos (2)}
  • First son of Kleomenes II
  • Brother of Kleonymos (1)
  • Father of Areus (1) Ib
  • He opposed the decree to relieve the survivors of the battle of Megalopolis, 331 BC, of ignominya.
  • He commanded the forces of Acragas in Sicily, ca. 314, against Agathokles, but he was stripped of his command and forced to return to Spartaa.
  • He predeceased his father (who died in 309 BC).b

Ἀκρότατος (2)

MID III BC

  • Athenaeus IV 142b; Parthenius 23; Plutarch Agis 3.7a, Pyrrhus 26.18b, 28.4-7c, Moralia (apophthegmata Laconica) 240ef}; Pausanias III 6.6; {VIII 27.11-13, VIII 30.7 by name refers to Akrotatos (1) but in fact refers to Akrotatos (2)}; SIG3 430d (The editor assigns this inscription to Areus <1> and Akrotatos <1>, but the reference to “King” Akrotatos and “Queen” Chilonis seems to me rather to refer to this Akrotatos.)
  • Son of Areus (1) Ia
  • Husband of Chilonis (1)
  • Father of Areus (2) IId
  • Agiad kinga
  • Supposedly he committed adultery with the wife of his great uncle, Kleonymos (1), shaming him into leaving Spartab, a story which overlies the intense and bitter rivalry between the families of Areus I and Kleonymos.
  • He was a young man during Pyrrhus’ invasion of Laconia, 272 BC, but he took part in the fightingc.
  • He led the Lacedaemonian army to Megalopolis and was killed there, ca. 262 BC, by Aristodemos, the tyranta.

Ἀλκαθόα

END VI BC

  • Poralla 55; Scholia to Aristophanes Equites 84; Suidas s. v. Παυσανίας (Ἀγειθέα); Polyaenus VIII 51 (Θεανώ); Diodorus XI 45,6; Nepos Pausanias 5,3
  • Mother of Pausanias and so also the mother of Nikomedes and wife of Kleombrotos. The different forms of the name most likely refer back to one form with 9 or 9. She is supposed to have brought a brick when her son Pausanias was in the temple of Athena Chalkioikos to wall him up.

Ἀλκαμένης

VIII BC

  • Poralla 56; Herodotus VII 204; Pausanias III 2.7, IV 4.4; FGrH (Apollodorus Chronika) II 244 (86/7)
  • Agid king
  • Son of Teleklos and father of Polydoros.
  • The chronographers made him an older contemporary of Theopompos and concluded that the First Messenian War began under him. His reign was supposed to have been 32 years long, 785/4-754/3.

Ἀλκαμένης

MID V BC

  • Poralla 57; Thucydides VIII 5, 8, 10
  • Son of the ephor Sthenlaidas, led an army in 412 to king Agis II at Decelea. He was supposed to sail a fleet to Chios but he was repulsed by the Athenians at the Peiraeus and in the following battle was killed.

  • [e] A. M.Woodward ABSA 26, 1923-25, 211-12 no. 10 with facsimile (XI 802)
  • [f] The same [?] should be postulated as father of P. Aelius Damocratidas in IG V 1. 655 (emended by L. Robert, REA 31, 1929, 13-18 and supplemented with two fragments by A. M. Woodward, ABSA 29, 1927-28, 41-43 no 65 with facsimile [XI 831], Spawforth, ABSA 79, 1984, 273
  • Remarks: Bradford distinguishes [1. 2f] [= p. 26 (2) from the Alcandridas of [2a-e] [= p. 27 (6)] regarding the latter as th grandfather of the former, whom he identifies with P. Aelius Alcandridas (III), son of Damocratidas, the prominent Spartan athlete and magistrate of the 1st half of the 3rd c. AD. This is rejected by A. J. S. Spawforth ABSA 80, 1985, 246, 247 n. 147, because he dates [1] in the 3rd quarter of the 2nd c. AD. He considers [1. 2a-e] as P. Aelius Alcandridas (II), the grandfather of P. Aelius Alcandridas (III). Settipani, 496 places his lifetime from AD 130 to after AD 155/65.
  • For the board of agranomoi in [1] see A. S. Bradford Chiron 10, 1980, 416 n. 33 and N. M. Kennell ZPE 85, 1991, 135n. 15.
  • Perhaps s. P. Aelius Nicandridas (LAC 16) and probably grands. P. Aelius Alcandridas (I) (LAC 5), presumably h. Pompeia Polla (I) (LAC 613) by whom f. P. Aelius Damocrates (LAC 9), grandf. P. Aelius Alcandridas (III) (LAC 7), perhaps also natural grandf. Ti. Claudius Aelius Partolaus (II) also known as Damocratidas (LAC 251); cf. stemmata in A. J. S. Spawforth, ABSA 80, 1985, 246 tab. 6 (Aelii Alcandridas and Settipani, 496 (the most important families of Roman Sparta); see infra, Appendix, Stemmata I and II.

  • =

Π(όπλιος) Αἴλιος [Ἀλκανδρί]δα[ς]

REIGN OF HADRIAN

  • Steinhauer, BSA 93, pp. 427-447, #3, plate 72a SEG 48, 1998, 457, l. 6;
  • AnnEpigr 1998, 1240 [AD 136/37]
  • Bo[uagos]
  • Gerousias [for the second or more time] in the year of Nike[phoros h]o [Markou].
  • “Remarks: The date of the first is based on prosopographical considerations (Woodward loc. cit and A. J. S. Spawforth, ABSA 80, 1985, 210-11 n. 69). Which leads A. M. Woodward to restore the lost name of the eponymous official by analogy with IG V 1. 63 ll. 16-17, a catalogue of ephors in the term of C. Julius Eudamos, A. J. S. Spawforth, ABSA 80, 1985, 27 convincingly restores [Πό(πλιος) Αἴλ(ιος)] Ἀλκ[ανδ]ρίδας β[ουαγός] in [1. 1.16]. If this restoration is correct, prosopographically he is the earliest known and otherwise unattested member of this family with Roman citizenship, hence P. Aelius Alcandridas (1). Considering the chronological evidence of this inscription, it is most likely that he had become a Roman citizen through a personal grant of Hadrian on the occasion of one of the emperor’s two visits at Sparta (in AD 124/5 and 128/9). Cf. W. Weber, Untersuchungen zur Geschichte des Kaisers Hadrianus (Leipzig 1907)188-89 n. 671. 211 ns. 744-45; H. Box JRS 21 1931, 201; Chrimes Ancient Sparta 465; Halfmann Itinera principum, 137, 192; Cartledge and Spawforth 108. This would mean that Alcandridas was already of advanced age when ensitos.
  • “An unpublished inscription discussed in Steinhauer Eurykles testifies that C. Julius Eurykles Herculanus (LAC 462, ARC 105) died in the patronomate of (C. Julius) Nicephoros son of Marcus attested in [2], which should be dated to ca. AD 136/7, see G. Steinhauer, ABSA 93, 1998, 431 n 9. This date allows the identification of P. Aelius Alcandridas in [2] with the homonymous person in [1].
  • “For the nature of the post and title of bouagos [1(?), 2] in the Spartan agoge of the Roman imperial period see Cartledge and Spawforth, esp 203-204; Kennell, Institutions, 181-85 and id., Gymnasium esp 41-42, 108-09. Perhaps f. P. Aelius Nikandridas (LAC 16) see stemma in Spawforth, op. cit., 246 tab 6 (Aelii Alcandridae); see infra, Appendix, Stemma II.”

Ἀλκίδας

MID V BC

  • Poralla 62; Thucydides III 16, 26, 29-33a, 69, 76-81b, 92c; Diodorus XII 55.6d
  • Nauarch of the year 428/7
  • He was supposed to relieve Mytilene in the spring of 427, but he delayed so much on the trip, that at Delos the news reached him of the fall of Mytilene.
  • After a few voyages here and there along the coast of Asia Minor, he met a superior Athenian force and fled back to the Peloponnesusad. From Cyllene (where Brasidas was his military adviser) he sailed to Corcyra in the summer of 427.
  • After an indecisive sea battle he escaped from the Athenian fleet over the Isthmus of Leukasb.
  • In 426 Alkidas went as founder to Herakleia in Trachisc.

Ἀλκίδας

V\IV BC

  • Poralla 63; Diodorus XV 46.1-3
  • Nauarch of the year 374/3. He was apparently despatched to Sicily and
  • on the way was supposed to ravage Corcyra. The attack miscarried.

Ἀλκίδας

  • Eusebius Chronicorum Libri II (ed. A. Schoene), I, 207, 208
  • Victor in the stadion during the 134th Olympiad

Ἀλκμάν

LATER VII BC

  • Poralla 67; Bergk Poetae Lyrici Graeci III p 46, fr 24a; Herakleides Pontikos II 2 in Müller, Fragmenta Historicorum Graecorum, Paris, 1878, II p 210b; Suidas s. v.c; Anthologia Palatina VII 19, 709d; SEG XXIX 388 (S. E. Waywell, American Journal of Archaeology, 83 <1979>, 303, #49): mosaic portrait bust, associated with Sappho and Anacreone; Aelian varia historia XII 50; The Partheneion (D. L. Page), Oxford, 1951; Alcmani, I frammenti (Antonio Garzya), Naples, 1954; Antonio Farina, Studi sul Partenio di Alcmane, Naples, 1950; Athenaeus I 31cd, II 39a, III 81d, f, 110f, 111a, 114f, 115a, IV 140c, IX 373e, 374d, 390a, X 416cd, XI 498f-499a, XIII 600f, XIV 624b, [636d], 637a, 638e, 646a, 648b, XV 678c, 680f, 681a, XV 682a; Pausanias I 41.4, III 15.2, 3, 18.6, 26.2; Plutarch Lycurgus 28.10, Sulla 36.5, Moralia (de fortuna Romanorum) 318a, (de exilio 2) 599e, (quaestionum convivalium II 10.2) 659b, ( de Herodoti malignitate 14) 857f, ( aetia physica 24) 918a, ( de facie in orbe lunae ) 940a; Aristotle historia animalium 557a2; PW Supplement XI 19-29
  • The poet of Laconian choral lyric from the second half of the seventh century. Over his antecedents there is no agreement. (1) Alcman came from Sardisa. Added to that is the reference that Alcman was the slave of the Lacedaemonian Agesidasb. (2) Elsewherec the poet is described as Λάκων ἀπὸ Μεσσόας and is given Damas or Titaros as his father. (3) Alexander the Aetoliand takes a middle position in an epigram; he holds Alcman for a Laconian, but says that his ancestors came from Sardis. In a mosaic portrait bust Alcman was associated with Sappho and Anacreone.

Ἀμομφάρητος

ca. 508-479 BC

  • Poralla 73; Herodotus IX 53-57, 71, 85; Plutarch Aristides 17
  • Son of Poliades
  • In 479 he fought in the battle of Plataea as leader of the Pitanatans and fell there, before he was 30 years old. His initial refusal to obey the command to retreat before the Persians brought on the battle. He was judged to be the bravest of the Spartans.

Ἀναξάνδρα

PRE-LITERATE

  • Poralla 79; Pausanias III 16.6
  • Daughter of the mythical king Thersandros of Kleonai, twin sister of Lathria
  • The pair were married to the sons of Aristodemos, Eurysthenes and Prokles.

Ἀναξανδρίδας I

VII\VI BC

  • Poralla 80; Herodotus VIII 131
  • King from the house of the Eurypontids
  • Son of king Theopompos
  • Father of Archidamos I
  • His reign falls at the turn of the seventh century.

Ἀναξανδρίδας II

MID VI BC

  • Poralla 81; Plutarch Moralia (apophthegmata Laconica s. v.
  • Ἀναξανδρίδας) 216f-217b; Herodotus I 67-8, V 39-41; Pausanias
  • III 3.5-6, 9
  • King from the house of the Agids
  • Son of king Leon
  • In his first marriage he wed the daughter of his sister. Childless, he was compelled to take a second wife (the daugher of Prinetadas), by whom he had the later king Kleomenes I. By his first wife he then had Dorieus, Leonidas, and Kleombrotos.
  • Anaxandridas was the contemporary of Croesus and Ariston. He reigned from about 550-516.
  • Under him the long war with Tegea was ended.

Ἀνάξανδρος

VII BC

  • Poralla 82; Herodotus VII 204; Pausanias III 3.4-5, 14.4, IV 15ff
  • King from the house of the Agids
  • Son of Eurykrates
  • Father of Eurykratidas
  • His wife’s name was Leandris. Pausanias puts him in the time of thesecond Messenian war.

Ἀνάξανδρος

END V BC

  • Poralla 83; Olymp 327; Pausanias VI 1.7
  • He was a victor in the Olympic games (Olympiad 88 = 428 BC ?) with the four horse chariot where also his father’s father had won in the Pentathlon.

Ἀνάξανδρος

MID IV BC

  • Poralla 84; Diodorus XVI 39.6
  • Around 351 as leader of a Spartan detachment he was captured by the allied Thebans and Argives near Telphusa

Ἀναξίβιος (Ϝαναξίβιος)

VI BC

  • Poralla 85; IG V 1. 215
  • Retrograde inscription: a dedication

Ἀναξίβιος

V\IV BC

  • Poralla 86; Xenophon Anabasis a V 1.4, VI 1.16, VII 1.10-20 2.4-8;
  • Hellenica IV 8.32-39b; Diodorus XIV 30.4c
  • Nauarch of the year 401/400.
  • In the spring of 400 he and his fleet were at Byzantium. He attempted to hinder the 10,000 from crossing into Europe (with one eye on the Persians)ac.
  • Around 389/8 he came to the Hellespont as harmost of Abydos. He was caught there by Iphicrates’ expedition to Abydos and fell in battleb.

Ἀναξίδαμος

VII BC

  • Poralla 87; Pausanias III 7.6, IV 15.3
  • Collateral relative of the house of the Eurypontids
  • Son of Zeuxidamos
  • Father of an Archidamos.
  • According to the suspect list of Pausanias he was king at the end of the second Messenian war.

Ἀναξίλας

  • Father of Leotychidas I
  • He may have ruled about the middle of the seventh century.

Ἀνήριστος

Ἀνήριστος

MID V BC

  • Poralla 95; Thucydides II 67; Herodotus VII 134, 137
  • Son of Sperthias
  • He was instrumental in the campaign at Halieis, perhaps in 459, against the Athenians.
  • In 430 he went to the king of Thrace Sitalkes to try to win him over to the Spartan side, but he was taken prisoner by Sadokos, the son of Sitalkes and handed over to the Athenians who executed him.

Ἀνταλκίδας

V\IV BC

  • Poralla 97; Plutarch Artaxerxes 21-22a; Agesilaus 23b, 32c; Xenophon Hellenica IV 8.12-16d; V 1.6, 25-29, 36e; VI 3.12f; Diodorus XIV 110g; Athenaeus II 48e; David Whitehead, Liverpool Classical Monthly IV (1979), 191-193, on the form of the name
  • Son of Leona
  • His mother was probably Teleutia.
  • In winter 393/2 he travelled to Sardis to the satrap Tiribazos from whom he received money for support of the fleetd. As nauarch of the year 388/7 he sailed from Aigina to Ephesus and betook himself to the Great King with whom he worked out the terms of the peace named after himeg.
  • After that he relieved Nikolochos who had been shut up in Abydose.
  • At the time of the 371 peace conference in Sparta he was spending time at the court of the Persian kingf.
  • In 370/69 he held the office of ephorc.
  • It was probably in 367 that he travelled for the third time to the king. There, however, when his mission was fruitless, he committed suicidea.

II-I BC

  • IG V 1. 1226
  • Father of Philon (2), a Lacedaemonian

Ἀντιάλκης

Ἄρακος

V/IV BC

  • Poralla 107; Xenophon Hellenica II 3.10.1a,7b; III 2.6-9c; VI 5.33d; Pausanias X 9.9e; Plutarch Lysander 7f; FDelph III I 51g (epigram)
  • Eponymous ephor of the year 409/8a. Nominal nauarch of the year 405/4b. In spring 398 with Naubates and Antisthenes he was sent to Dercylidas in Asia Minorc. In winter 370/69 he was an ambassador in Athensd. (But is the ambassador a second Arakos?)

Ἀράτα (1)

  • IG V 1. 579
  • Daughter of Tycharetos
  • Subject of an honorary decree for her sensible and pious life; dedication to Demeter and Kore

Ἀράτα (2)

MID IV BC

  • Poralla 108; IG IV2 122 xxi ( = SIG3 1169 xxi)
  • [La]kaina
  • A sufferer from dropsy. Her mother went to the shrine of Asclepius in Epidaurus to find a cure. In her sleep she saw Asclepius decapitate her daughter—a liquid flowed from her head—and he rejoined head and neck. The mother hurried home to Sparta, found her daughter cured, and the dream fulfilled.

Ἄρατος (2)

AFTER MID II BC

  • IG V 1. 961
  • Son of Nikias (16)
  • A Lacedaemonian honored by Cotyrta for his benefactions. He and his descendants were granted the rights of proxenos and benefactor: to own land and a house, to contract marriage, to have the protection of law, exemption, asylum in war and peace, and the other customary rights.

Ἄρευς (1) I

REIGN 309-265 BC

  • Diodorus Siculus XX 29.1a; Justin XXIV 1.5; Pompeius Trogus prologi 26; Pausanias I 13.5; III 6.2-6b; VI 12.5-6, 15.9; Plutarch Agis 3.6-7c, Pyrrhus 26.17-19d, 27.2e, 29.11f, 30.4, Moralia (apophthegmata Laconica) 217f g; Josephus Antiquitates Judaicae XII 225-27h, XIII 167 (9); 1 Maccabees 12.1-23; Athenaeus IV 142b; ICret II xxiii 12Ai; IOlymp 308j; IG IV 1. 332; SEG XXV 444k; SEG XI 668 (?—Dedication to Athena); [SIG3 430, see Areus (2) II]; Grunauer, pp. 112-113 (Gr. I-II, Tafel 1: ΒΑΣΥΛΕΟΣ ΑΡΕΟΣ)
  • Son of Akrotatos (1)
  • Grandson of Kleomenes II
  • Father of Akrotatos (2), king of Sparta
  • Agiad king of Spartaa, 309-265 BCbc
  • He succeeded to the throne despite the fact that Kleonymos (1), son of Kleomenes II, was alive. Kleonymos, however, was given command of the armies. Their rivalry, intensified, no doubt, by Akrotatos’ adultery with the wife of Kleonymos, led to Kleonymos’ leaving Sparta and joining Pyrrhus.bd
  • Areus was an active king, forming connections in Sicilyg, Creteei, Egyptjk, and possibly Judaeah.
  • He attempted to restore the Spartan hegemony of the Peloponnesus and opposed the Macedonian forces in Greece, although he was forced into a brief alliance with them to forestall the invasion of Pyrrhus into Laconiaf.
  • He was killed in an attempt to force the Macedonian lines at Corinth, 265 BCc

Ἄρευς (2) II

262-254 BC

  • SIG3 430; Pausanias III 6.6; Plutarch Agis 3.7-8; [Pyrrhus 26.17-18]
  • In SIG3 430 the Delphians grant proxenia to “King Areus, son of King Akrotatos and Queen Chilonis.” The editor believes that this refers to Areus I, since it seemed unlikely to him that the Delphians would grant proxenia to a child, albeit a king. Akrotatos, however, the father of Areus I, was not a king. There is but one king Akrotatos and he is the father of Areus II. Moreover, the Chilonis of the inscription might well be the widow of Kleonymus and lover of Akrotatos the king [26.17-18].)
  • Son of Akrotatos (2) and Chilonis (1)
  • Grandson of Areus (1) I
  • He was born after the death of his father at Megalopolis, 262 BC. Leonidas (1), the son of Kleonymos (1), was regent. He was an Agiad king.
  • He died of disease when he was eight years old.

Ἄρευς (3)

III\II BC

  • Livy XXXIX 35-37; Pausanias VII 9.2-4; Polybius XXII 1.9 & 11.7-12.4; XXIII 4.3
  • Of royal descent?
  • He was exiled from Sparta by Nabis and restored against the wishes of the government of Sparta by the Achaean league.
  • In 184 BC he was an envoy to the Romans and he denounced the Achaean league.

He and his descendants were granted the status of proxenos and benefactor with the right to hold land and a house, to have legal recourse, asylum in war and peace, to be invited to the public festivals, to have the major rights of hospitality and the other customary rights

Ἀριστόδαμος

V\IV BC

  • Poralla 126; Plutarch Moralia (narrationes amatoriae 3) 773b-774d (cf. Xenophon Hellenica V 4.56/7)
  • Harmost in Oreus
  • According to the story in Plutarch he. must have been harmost before the battle at Leuctra. In this period a harmost could have been in Oreus only after the fall of Athens and before the sack of Oreus in 377/6 by Alketas.

Ἀριστόκριτος

V BC

  • Poralla 129; Plutarch Lysander 2; IG II2 1388 line 32, 1400 line 15; Pausanias VI 3.14; Xenophon Hellenica II 4.28; Diodorus XIV 13.5/6

Ἀριστομενίδας

V\IV BC

  • Poralla 134; Pausanias III 9.3
  • Belonged to the Spartan court of five men who sentenced the Plataeans to death in 427. In 396 he was sent as ambassador to Thebes.
  • Pausanias says that he was the father of the mother of Agesilaos, which is totally impossible (because of the dates). He may have been the father-in-law of Agesilaos, that is the father of Kleora. Or the name of the father of the mother of Agesilaus may have been Aristomenidas, but a different person. See Μελησιππίδας.

Ἀριστοτέλης

V\IV BC

  • Poralla 137; Diodorus XIV 78.1
  • He was a leader of mercenaries with Dionysius of Syracuse. Because of his ambiguous attitude towards Dionysius he was arrested in 396 and sent to Sparta for judgement.

Ἀρίστων

MID VI BC

  • Poralla 138; Herodotus I 67, VI 61-63; Pausanias III 7.7-8; Plutarch Moralia (apophthegmata Laconica s.v.) 218ab
  • King from the house of the Eurypontids
  • Son of Agasikles
  • Because his first two marriages were childless, he married a third time ... the wife of his friend Agetos. From this marriage came the later king Damaratos. Ariston was a contemporary of Croesus and Anaxandridas. While he was king the long war against Tegea was ended.

Ἀρχιδάμια

DIED 241 BC

  • Plutarch Agis 4.1a, 20.3b, Pyrrhus 27.4-5c; Polyaenus VIII 49d
  • Daughter of King “Kleadas” = Kleomenes II?d
  • Wife of Eudamidas {(1) I?}
  • Mother of Agesistrata, Agesilaos (2), {and Archidamos (2) IV?}b
  • Grandmother of Agis (1) IV, Archidamos (3) <V>, and Hippomedon (1)a <Polybius (IV 35.13) states that Hippomedon was in the line of Eurypontid succession, which would be readily understandable if he were the grandson of a king. Agesilaos, his father, was the son of a Eudamidas. Eudamidas I was a Eurypontid. It seems likely then that Archidamia was the wife of Eudamidas I.>
  • During the invasion of Laconia by Pyrrhus, 272 BC, Archidamia opposed a plan to send the women and children of Sparta to Crete. She organized the women to fortify the city, carry weapons, and treat the wounded. She aided and encouraged the Spartan soldiers.c
  • She was one of the wealthiest women in Sparta, but she supported the reforms of Agis IV with both her money and her influence.a
  • She was executed after his fall in 241 BCb

Ἀρχιδαμίδας

IV\III BC?

  • Poralla 153; Plutarch Moralia (apophthegmata Laconica s. v.) 218b; Lycurgus 20
  • A Spartiate contemporary of Hecataeus (of Abdera?)—he responded to a criticism of Hecataeus and to a question about the number of Spartiates

Ἀρχίδαμος I

  • Poralla 154; Herodotus VIII 131
  • King from the Eurypontid house
  • Son of Anaxandridas
  • Father of Anaxilas

Ἀρχίδαμος

  • Poralla 155; Pausanias III 7.5
  • According to the false kings’ list of Pausanias he was a king from the Eurypontid house, son of Theopompos and father of Zeuxidamos. He is supposed to have died before his father. Perhaps to be identified with Archidamos (Poralla 154).

Ἀρχίδαμος

  • Poralla 156; Pausanias III 7.6
  • According to the false kings’ list of Pausanias he was a king from the Eurypontid house and son of Anaxidamos and father of Agasikles

Ἀρχίδαμος II

MID V BC

  • Poralla 157; Plutarch Agesilaus 1a, 2.6; Herodotus VI 71b; Xenophon Agesilaus 9.6c, Hellenica V 2.3d; Pausanias III 7.10e, 15.1f, VI 1.6g; Diodorus XI 63.4-64.1h, XII 42.6-8i, 47.1-2j; Thucydides II 10-12k, 18-23l, 47m, 71-78n, III 1o; Libanius declamationes 20.19; Athenaeus XIII 566a
  • King from the house of the Eurypontids
  • Son of Zeuxidamos
  • Father of Agis II (from his first marriage with his step-aunt Lampido)ab and Agesilaos II and Kyniska (by his second wife Eupolia)acfg
  • When shortly before 476 Leotychidas had to go into exile at Tegea, his grandson Archidamos assumed the rulee. Whether he had already taken part in the battles of Tegea in 473 and Dipaia can not be known. He was first mentioned in the great earthquake in Sparta in 464, where he saved the state through his presence of mindh. He distinguished himself in the ensuing battles against the Messeniansd.
  • Archidamos commanded the first invasion of Attica in the year 431 and 430klm. In 429 he took Plataea and in the next year led an army into Attica for the third time.no
  • He became sick and died at the latest in the Winter 427/6.

Ἀρχίδαμος III

DIED 338 BC

  • Poralla 158; SEG XI 457 (treaty with [Ach]aeans); Xenophon Hellenica V 4.25a, VI 4.18-19b, 26c, VII 1.28-32d, 4.20-25e, 5.12-13f; Plutarch Agis 3g, Agesilaus 19h, 33i, 34j, 40k; Camillus 19.8l; Pausanias III 10.3-5m, VI 4.9n; Arrian Anabasis II 13.6o; Isocrates Epistulae IX (Archidamos)p; Diodorus XVI 24q, 39r, 59s, 62-63, 88u; Aeschines II 133v; Athenaeus VII 289e, XII 536cd, XIII 591b w; Libanius orationes 64.83; declamationes (Archidami defensio) XXIV passim
  • King from the house of the Eurypontids (born about 400)
  • Son of Agesilaos II and Kleora.
  • Brother of Eupolia and Prolytaah
  • Husband of Deinicha
  • Father of Agis III, Eudamidas I and Agesilaosgmo
  • In 371 he led the defeated army of Kleombrotos back from Megara to Sparta. (Diodorus XV 54-55 in error puts Archidamos also at the battle of Leuctra.)bc
  • In the years 367 and 364 Archidamos campaigned against the Arcadians in the fielddei.
  • Isokrates put a speech in his mouth that he was supposed to have delivered at the Peace Congress in Sparta in 366/5p.
  • In 362 he was occupied in the defense of Sparta against the Thebansfj.
  • After the death of Agesilaos II in the winter of 360/59 he ascended the thronek.
  • At the outbreak of the Sacred War Archidamos in secret helped the Phociansmq. Around 352 he fought against Megalopolisr, and in 346 led an army to help Phocis, but because of the ambiguities of the situation among the Phocian leaders returned to Sparta with nothing accomplishedsv.
  • After that he was sent to Italy to help Tarentum in a war against the Lucanians. He sailed first to Crete where he refounded Lyttos. In Italy he fought a battle at Mandonion 338—on the seventh of the month Metageitnionl—lost the battle and his lifegmtuv.
  • He had a portrait bust in Olympian and a statue in Delphiw.

Ἀρχίδαμος (2) IV

DIED 294 BC?

  • Plutarch Agis 3.3a; Demetrius 35.1b; [Polyaenus IV 7.9-10]c; [Pausanias II 8.5; III 10.5; VII 7.3; VIII 8.11, 10.5-8, 27.13-14, 36.6 confuses Archidamos and Agis (1) IV and perhaps other kings]
  • Son of Eudamidas (1) I {and Archidamia}a
  • {Brother of Agesistrata and Agesilaos (2)}
  • Father of Eudamidas (2) IIa
  • {Grandfather of Agis IV, Archidamos (3) <V>, and Hippomedon (1)}
  • Eurypontid king
  • He fought a battle with Demetrius near Mantinea, where he was defeated, 294 BCbc There is no further mention of Archidamos in the sources and he may have been killed in this battle.

Ἀρχίδαμος (3) {V}

DIED 227 BC

  • Polybius IV 35.13a; V 37.1-5b; VIII 35.3-5c; Plutarch Cleomenes 1.1d; 5.2-4e; comparatio Agis Cleomenes Ti. Gracchus C. Gracchus 5.2f
  • Son of Eudamidas (2) II and Agesistrata
  • Brother of Agis (1) IVe
  • First cousin and son-in-law of Hippomedon (1)a
  • Father of two sons, names unknowna
  • Upon the execution of his brother he fled into exile in Messene and lived there until he was persuaded by Kleomenes (1) III to return and become the Eurypontid kingbdef. When he returned, he was murderedbcef.
  • Whether he actually became king is unclear.

END V BC

  • Poralla 167; Pausanias X 9.9

  • that Antipater could not prevent them from dying for Sparta

Ἀστύοχος

END V BC

  • Poralla 169; Thucydides VIII 20, 23, 31-45, 61-63, 78-84
  • Nauarch of the year 412/11
  • His activity as nauarch was between Chios, Lesbos, Miletus, and Cnidos. He aroused resistence to himself in Sparta and among his own soldiers and mishandled Persian relations so that the Spartans had to send a committee to watch over him

Ἀψίνης

IV AD

  • Eunapius vitae Sophistarum Julianus 482-485
  • “From Lacedaemon”
  • A sophist in Athens and a rival of Julianus the sophist
  • (His students, because of their rough ways, were called Laconians, which may have led to his being labelled a Lacedaemonian.)
